{"id": "8a66aa7e", "body": "", "comments": [{"timstamp": "2015-09-02 17:43", "user": "russruss:", "body": "Hey all, is it safe to embed v8 in a dynamically loaded plug-in that will run in a host app that may or may not have its own copy of v8? I understand isolates, but Im worried about v8-owned global state. Ill often be running on the same os thread as the host app, if that matters"}, {"timstamp": "2015-09-02 17:44", "user": "russruss:", "body": "Im willing to be as careful as necessary in the loaded plug-in :-P"}, {"timstamp": "2015-09-02 17:44", "user": "russruss:", "body": "could you provide some hints on what to look out for?"}, {"timstamp": "2015-09-02 17:44", "user": "Torne:", "body": "in that case you will need to ensure that the plugin doesn't have any dynamic symbols that are related to V8"}, {"timstamp": "2015-09-02 17:44", "user": "Torne:", "body": "since these would be at risk of being masked by symbols defined by the host application"}, {"timstamp": "2015-09-02 17:45", "user": "Torne:", "body": "you'd want to make sure your plugin *only* exports symbols that are unrelated to V8 and that the host app is expecting to call"}, {"timstamp": "2015-09-02 17:46", "user": "Torne:", "body": "as long as when your plugin is linked all the V8 symbols are resolved by the linker locally and not allowed to be dynamic/exported such that they coul be changed by the dynamic linker at load time, you should be okay"}, {"timstamp": "2015-09-02 17:47", "user": "Torne:", "body": "if you're doing this on a non-windows OS note that in a normal *nix shared library, *all* the symbols are dynamic by default and you have to explicitly prevent them from being so ;)"}, {"timstamp": "2015-09-02 17:51", "user": "Torne:", "body": "if you want more specific advice you may want to ask the v8-users mailing list"}, {"timstamp": "2015-09-02 17:52", "user": "Torne:", "body": "but the above is what i know about symbols/linking that's relevant ;)"}, {"timstamp": "2015-09-02 18:01", "user": "russruss:", "body": "Torne: thanks! sounds a bit hairy actually"}, {"timstamp": "2015-09-02 18:11", "user": "Torne:", "body": "russruss: it's relatively easy if you understand dynamic linking on the platform(s) you are targeting, it's just annoying"}, {"timstamp": "2015-09-02 18:12", "user": "Torne:", "body": "e.g. on systems like linux that use ELF, -fvisibility=hidden as a gcc arg will make every symbol hidden by default and you can mark the symbols you intend to expose as having visibility default with a function attribute"}, {"timstamp": "2015-09-02 18:12", "user": "Torne:", "body": "google for symbol visibility etc and you should find out a bunch of stuff :)"}], "label": "other"}
